text:
Wow!  I've never cooked chicken this juicy and delicious before!  I made a few changes to this recipe.  I used plain bread crumbs and added a generous teaspoon of Italian seasoning.  I nixed the rice crispies - only because that's the only ingredient that I didn't have on hand.  I decided against adding melted butter on top of the chicken (I figured there was enough fat already with the cheese).  I also baked at 350 for 45 minutes - I've found that the trick to juicy baked boneless skinless chicken breasts is to bake them at exactly this temp and length of time.  My husband (who is picky about food) actually said "wow" when he saw the finished product.  He also specifically asked that I add this dish into my dinner rotation.  Bravo!  This was a HUGE hit!  I served it with steamed brocolli, pineapple casserole (will post this recipe soon), and garlic parmesean biscuits (will post this recipe soon as well).

text:
I have already rated this recipe once before with 5 stars.  I just wanted to say that I made it for 17 people when my fiancee' and I went to the beach with his family and my family. There were a few very picky eaters in the bunch but this recipe was a success with them.  I cooked 24 pieces of the cheddar chicken for dinner one night and I think there were only 2 or 3 left over.  They were very quickly warmed up and eaten for lunch the next day.  This is one of the best chicken recipes I have ever used.  I would give it 10 stars if I could.

text:
Wonderful! I did make a couple of changes to the original recipe though - 1)I used shredded asiago cheese instead of cheddar 2)I baked it for 45 minutes as suggested by others 3) I used Crispix cereal since that was all I had 4) I dredged the raw chicken thru sour cream before the flour mix 5) I didn't use butter on the bottom of the pan, but did over the tops and then added a little more topping. Turned out amazing... my whole family loved it. I served it with noodles and alfredo sauce, but it would be excellent with spaghetti and marinara too. We'll be having this one again!!

text:
My boyfriend took one bite of this and said "5 stars all the way!". This was SO GOOD! Followed the recipe except I put the garlic powder, salt, and pepper directly on the chicken before dredging it in the flour. I also decided to skip putting all that butter in the bottom of the dish... just sprayed it liberally with nonstick cooking spray. Baked 35 minutes and then broiled it for 3-4 minutes to give it a nice crispy top. Served with mashed potatoes and garlic green beans for a very tasty meal! Thank you!!!

text:
I made this chicken dish, along with herbed wild rice and fresh steamed greenbeans, in less than 45 minutes. Not only was it quick and simple to prepare (had most ingredients on hand anyway), but the chicken was delicious! It was juicy on the inside and crunchy on the outside - I did put the oven on broil for 2 minutes after the 35 minute cooking time was through just to get the tops a little more browned. It's also great as leftovers, heated up or sliced chilled and thrown into a salad. And it can be made into a lower fat dish just by substituting out the cheese for low-fat and cutting down on the butter a little or all together: spray the pan with Pam or grease lightly with olive oil, and omit the butter drizzle. Thanks for the new simple and versatile chicken dish!

Crispy on the outside, juicy on the inside. Kids ate - yeah! I used panko bread crumbs in place of the rice krispies, and plain breadcumbs instead of flavored (this was what I had on hand). I used low fat Cheddar and put a little bit of olive oil on the baking sheet in place of the butter to cut back on the fat. Even with the minor substitutions it was very tasty and I will make again. Also, very good the next day - cold - on a salad with low fat honey mustard dressing.

text:
I made this recipe tonight after reading all of the previous reviews.  The suggestions of others that I followed were these: spray the pan instead of coating with butter, filet thick pieces of chicken, make less of the coating to avoid lots of leftover (I halved all of the dry ingredients), bake for 45 minutes instead of 35, and partially crush the cereal.  My own changes were to cut the chicken into more pieces and to use a frosted corn flake cereal.  Everybody here LOVED it.

text:
This recipe turned out well.  I served it with brown rice and french-cut green beans.  My fiance' enjoyed it overall.  He said it was very moist and had a different flavor.  
However, there are a few things I'll tweak for the next time I make it.  Instead of butter, I'll use a spray oil, such as Pam, on the pans.  The butter didn't coat the pans as well as I would have liked and I had to keep adding oil so the chicken wouldn't stick.
In addition, I would increase the oven temperature.  I have a gas oven and normally have it set between 425-450* F and adjusting as needed.  350* F was way too slow and I had to increase just for dinner to be done in a timely manner.
I would also add a bit more flavor.  As well as more cheese.  It was a little bland at first and you couldn't taste the cheese.
Overall, this is a good recipe and we will have it again someday soon.  :)

text:
A new family favorite!  I had no intention of altering this recipe but when I went to make it, I was doubling the recipe and then found that I was a bit short on garlic powder.  I altered the spices a bit and used McCormick's Original Chicken Seasoning which has garlic powder in it.  I adjusted the other spices accordingly and also added some white pepper.  Any of the breast pieces which were over an inch thick, I filleted so that the cooking time would even out.  I baked at 350 for 30 minutes in an industrial convection oven and it was perfect.  There was no need to broil in order to brown the outside. I regretfully did not drizzle the butter over the top.  I had poured the remaining cheese crust breading on top and I think  this would have been perfect if I had of drizzled the butter or perhaps added a bit more cheddar cheese to add some moisture to the breading.  The breading was excellent except in areas that lacked cheese and then it was a bit powdery.  Also I crushed the rice crispies a bit before adding to the mix as I couldnt see how it would stick well otherwise.  All in all an excellent answer to what to do with the frozen boneless breasts in the freezer.  My family of six are waiting to have this one again.

text:
OMG!! I did make a few alterations...as in adding some different spices, but it was to die for! I normally make 4 pieces of chicken for dinner. It's just my husband and I, so if the chicken is good, we will split half of one of the extra breasts and then he will have an leftover one to take to work the next day. This was so awesome, we both ate 2 breasts!! Unheard of...lol 

The alterations I made were: I didn't have the crispy cereal so I omitted it. When I mixed up the flour mixture I added in cumin since I would be using a Mexican blend shredded cheese (thought I would incorporate some Mexican into the chicken), extra garlic and a shake or two of chayenne pepper to give it a bit of spice. I had Italian bread crumbs, but since I was going for the "Mexican" flavor, I used roasted garlic bread crumbs instead.

It turned out soo fantastic! The yellow rice I paired it with paled in comparison!!

text:
Very tasty dish! Since I have such a large family, I upped the amount of servings to 8, and then used 6 chicken breasts. This worked out just fine, because after I was done with all the coating/rolling, the only thing I didn't have extra of was the egg/milk mixture. I did make a couple of slight changes...I omitted the butter on the bottom of the pan, and sprayed it generously with cooking spray. I didn't have any Italian bread crumbs, so I crumbled up some dry bread in a pan, baked it until it was crispy, crushed it fine, and added some garlic salt, parsley flakes, dried oregano, and dried basil. Other than that, I made this exactly as written. It took a little longer to bake, but boy was it worth it! My family was skeptical when they first saw it, because the chicken does look a little unusual. They all enjoyed it though...thanks for sharing!

text:
Yummy.  As always I marinated my chicken breasts in buttermilk for a few hours..that makes for some MOIST chicken(if no buttermilk use milk with a few tsp white vinegar) I needed to make this dish in advance for the DH to just put in the oven when I was at work so- I didn't want to melt the butter so I just put pats of butter all along the bottom of a 13x9 dish and laid the chicken on top. (sorry but I did skip the flour and egg part too because when I took the chicken out of the buttermilk they were plenty moist to have the crumbs stick-plus who wants to dirty extra bowls anyway).   I also didn't mix my cheese with the crumbs I just covered the tops of the chicken with it adding on a few more pats of butter to each.  DELICIOUS.  Will keep this one in the rotation..great kid friendly dish(you can even get away with half the butter-it's not necessary).

This came out really delicious. I made it for my daughters who are extremely picky and they  loved it. I had to make small changes due to the fact that I have a  gluten allergy, so I did replace the regular flour with Red Mill's Gluten Free All Purpose Baking Flour and the bread crumbs with Nature's Promise GF Panko bread crumbs. Same measurements as the regular ingredients. I liked the idea of adding Italian seasoning to the bread crumbs as another reviewer had done and will try that next time because GF bread crumbs never come seasoned. I ended up cooking it for 40 minutes. I also used boneless, skinless chicken tenders only because that is what I had on hand and I didn't add the rice crispy cereal because I didn't have it. I LOVED the seasoning so much I even ate the seasoning that had browned and was left over in the pan, it was just that good. I'm so glad I made 2 extra pieces so I can have it for lunch tomorrow. Thanks for the recipe it will definitely go into my favorites.

text:
Per another reviewer I omitted the rice crispies (I didn't have them and really don't care for them).  I also had to season my bread crumbs and  omitted the extra butter on top.  I made one other change: After dredging in the flour I dipped the chicken again in the egg mixture then dipped in the breadcrumb mixture.  I think this makes the final coating stick better.  I also cooked the chicken for 45 minutes.  It was the most moist chicken breast ever!  I will make it again.

text:
I've made this recipe literally countless times by now.  I found it years ago and if you were to ask my kids what their favorite dish is they'll say "cheese chip chicken" which is what they call this for some reason.  I didn't read all the reviews since there are so many but if it hasn't been said yet, I want to advise anyone making this to:   -Cut their chicken in half if the breasts are super large.  -Bake for 45 minutes.  -Salt the chicken with rock salt before you begin the steps of dredging.  The chicken is extremely tasty and moist.  I wouldn't change a single ingredient.

This was delicious and juicy, even though I had my doubts, especially about the butter on the bottom of the dish. I did change it slightly to what I had on hand. I swapped the garlic powder for a little garlic salt and onion powder (how could I not have garlic powder, I have NO clue!), I used regular bread crumbs and mixed in a little over a tablespoon of Italian seasoning, and just ditched the cereal because I personally thought it might be slight over-kill on the crunchy. As for the butter, I used probably a little less than a teaspoon per each piece of chicken, only because I cut them into kid-sizes instead of huge pieces (the chicken breasts I had were pretty thick). However, all and all it was a keeper and my mom insisted this becomes a regular.

text:
I've been using this recipe for a few years now and it's ALWAYS a huge hit. Everyone that trys it loves this dish and I always have a least one person in the group ask for the recipe. 
Because I have to cook for so many people when I make it, I end up at least tripling the ingredients. I also sprinkle additional cheddar cheese on the bottom of the baking dish prior to placing the chicken in it. I also heavily sprinkle more cheese over the top of all the chicken once in the dish and drizzle anywhere from 1-2 additional tablespoons of butter over the chicken before placing it in the oven. The dish turns out much more cheesy (and fattening) than the original recipe. It's become my family & I's favorite chicken dish!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I made some changes though. I sprayed my baking dishes with non-stick spray rather than use all that butter. Instead of breasts I used legs and thighs. To the flour mixture I added a teaspoon of onion powder as well as chili powder. I think I will increase the amounts of garlic, onion and chili powders next time for a more prominent flavour. For the egg mixture, one egg would not have been enough for my chicken pieces so I used two and replaced the milk with two tablespoons of sour cream (didn't want to open a new bag of milk just for a few drops) which worked just fine, and probably added more to the chicken than the milk would have. I followed the coating to the letter, but I would like to suggest using a a strong cheddar so that the cheese can be noticed... All I had was a mild white cheddar and that wasn't strong enough. Definitely use the yellow cheddar, or if you prefer white, old or extra old. Many reviews chose not to drizzle on some butter before cooking but I went ahead and did... It's not necessary, as the it only makes the chicken greasy and adds unneeded calories. I cooked mine for 50 minutes, flipping halfway through to ensure even crispiness.

This was pretty good, although it really didn't crisp up as much as I would have liked in 35 minutes.  (Might be my oven.)  I did have to make a few changes for what I had on hand. I'd make it again.

I made this recipe pretty much as written, with three chicken breasts sliced in half and baked in a glass Pyrex dish.  I used crushed Crispex cereal instead of the rice crispies, and added sliced Parmesan cheese for some extra flavor. We ate two servings each night for dinner. The first night it was a bit bland, and I wished I had season the chicken itself before coating.  Reheated the second and third nights, though, after the flavors had time to blend, it was tasty+. I'd make this recipe again, but would season the chicken itself for some extra punch.

text:
Yes, this is good! I did not use butter, I used EV Olive Oil. I used Mexican Cheese Blend rather than cheddar.  I added Red Pepper Flakes to the Egg Wash and regular Bread Crumbs with a little Italian Seasoning. I used skinless boneless chicken breasts. I rinsed them clean and troweled dry; then I rubbed them completely with Olive Oil. I sprinkled Garlic Powder on all surfaces and lightly massaged it into the meat. I dredged them through the Flour Mixture, then the Egg Wash, then the final Crumb/Cereal/Cheese mix. Then I re-dredged them in the last of the Egg Wash and then the last of the Crumb/Cereal/Cheese mix. I used aluminum foil to line the baking dish and used Olive Oil to coat the foil. I baked them at 350 for about 35-minutes. They came out juicy and very flavorful.

This recipe is a little messy (3-bowls) but I cleaned up as I went along. The aluminum foil liner really speeds up final cleanup! We enjoyed these cheddar chicken breasts very much and I'll make them again.

Finally a delicious baked chicken.  I would have given it 5 stars but I did make some changes to the recipe.  It turned out moist, crunchy and delicious.  The leftovers eaten cold are even great.  My husband (who hates chicken and does not cook) loved this recipe.  I even caught him snacking on the leftovers, that never happens with chicken!

I have made it 3 times now and it turns out perfect every time.  I also used leftovers as chicken parmesan and it was delicious.

Also, don't know if it's just me, but the prep time took a lot longer than I had planned. Yes, I will make again.

text:
This is an easy recipe and it didn't disappoint!  I used seasoned panko bread crumbs instead of the Rice Crispies/ bread crumb mixture and they worked perfectly.  I also seasoned my boneless breasts (cut in half lengthwise) with salt and pepper and I also seasoned both the flour dredge and the bread crumb/cheese coating with a little seasoned salt, garlic power, onion powder, and black and cayenne pepper and pressed the chicken firmly in the final coating to ensure good adherence.  I cooked the chicken according to the recipe; exactly 25 minutes, and it resulted in a tender, juicy, and crispy piece of chicken...and boneless, skinless chicken breasts have a tendency to be dry if not timed perfectly.   One final thought; next time I might try a stronger-flavor cheese, as we couldn't really taste the colby- jack in the final product.  Perhaps a swiss or sharp cheddar would give a more pronounced flavor.  
Thanks for the recipeI will definitely use this one again and again!

text:
This was easy to prepare and delicious. After reading all the other reviews I cherry picked from several of their changes - - I used Italian panko breadcrumbs, halved the breading recipe for two large boneless chicken breasts (about 1.4 lbs total), which I seasoned with seasoned salt and pepper before breading, used Italian panko breadcrumbs and equal parts shredded mild cheddar and deli shredded parmesan cheese, omitted the cereal and tossed in a handful of French fried onion pieces as another reviewer did. I also didn't grease my baking dish at all, but did drizzle 1.5tbs butter over the breaded chicken, which I cooked for 45 minutes (perfect). I had very little breading left over after I added extra to the top and I would definitely make it this way again. Thanks for the great recipe!

country:

text:
This is a delicious & easy recipe!  I gave it 4 *s, only because I made a couple of changes.  I used crushed Corn Flakes instead of rice cereal, and I added quite a bit more garlic powder, dried parsley, onion powder, and Italian seasoning to the bread crumbs.... since I noticed that the seasonings have been greatly reduced in the store bought breadcrumbs (even in the 'brand names').  Here's a tip which always works:  Use a meat thermometer.  Insert it into the thickest part of the chicken breast.  Take the chicken out of the oven BEFORE it reaches an internal temperature of 160 deg.  (I take it out at about 158 deg.)  Then, put a loose 'tent' of aluminum foil over it, and let it 'rest' for several minutes (it will continue to cook) and when it reaches an internal temperature of 165 deg. it's ready (and safe) to eat.  I hope this info was helpful.

text:
As my kids would say "Winner, winner, chicken dinner". This came out moist, crispy, and flavorful. For once, I actually followed the recipe just as written. It was easy, quick, and best of all, made with things that I usually have in my house anyway. I would agree that you probably could cut down on the butter if you wanted, but you leave a lot of it in the dish when you take the chicken out, so I wouldn't bother to cut back and risk losing moisture. If I changed anything, I might cut back a little bit on the salt, but we don't use a lot of salt, so we may just like things less salty than most people. Really good chicken. Got requests from my teen-aged boys to make it again, so there's the real endorsement.

text:
Quite yummy. 

I didn't have cereal so I substituted croutons (garlic & herb) because I figured it would add enough crunch and still fit with the other flavors. I also had to cook it for 45 minutes like another reviewer said, but I had very thick chicken breasts so that was probably a factor.

It has nice crunch, the flavors mix well, and the chicken remained juicy and yummy. My only complaint would be that it's not overly seasoned...I'd probably add in more spices next time. I don't think that's the fault of my croutons because if anything that should have added more seasoning flavor.

This chicken was yummier than I expected! I didn't use any crispy rice cereal b/c I didn't have any. I used panko Italian bread crumbs and I did add my seasoning to the chicken, not the flour. I sliced my chicken breast into two so my chicken breast were thinner and I decided to roll my breast after I coated them in everything. I baked in my toaster oven on 300 for 40 mins. Then for another 10 mins, b/c some of the thicker pieces looked a little pink. I also did melt a little bit of butter in the baking dish and added some cut onion, then put the chicken on top. I also had extra bread crumb cheese mix so I just put it on top. Only thing I think I may change next time is to make thinner slices of breast and season a little bit more.

This is my first rating, and I'm so glad it was this particular recipe to set me of on the right foot!  My wife tends to "stick to what you know". I wanted to start with something simple and mild in flavor, but savory. This was an absolute hit!  I only changed a few things. Thank you for my first recipe, as it will now be a new part of our rotation!

text:
My husband has always been the chef in our home and has high standards.  Now that he is a cardiac patient and must follow low-sodium and low-fat rules, I find that I need to step in and step up.  This recipe is pretty good.  I did not not cut the breasts in half, and did fine with 350 for 40 minutes (convection style) and then low broiler for 5 minutes.  I might go ahead and try cutting them next time so we aren't waiting so long to eat the meal.
I didn't have rice cereal on hand.  I had canned bread crumbs on hand, both plain and seasoned: the sodium is way high.  What I used instead was my own concoction of AP flour, ground flaxseed, panko crumbs, and some crushed whole wheat crackers that had been sitting around and whose sodium was lower than the regular bread crumbs.  I added my own dried herbs and crushed them with mortar and pestle.  The chicken itself I seasoned generously with garlic powder, very lightly with crushed pink himalayan salt, and fresh ground black pepper.  In the glass casserole dish, I used high quality unsalted butter and smeared a thin layer to coat the bottom.  I did melt some of the same to drizzle on top.  
With it, I served a blend of couscous, quinoa, and veggies that came in a steamable bag in the frozen section.  I fully expected my husband to hate every bit of it.  We were both pleasantly surprised that it all turned out a rather delicious meal that we could feel good about.

text:
Made this last night for my picky teenage daughter and husband.  My husband is picky because he is a great cook himself, and often does the cooking in our household.  My daughter is picky because she is used to my husband's great cooking.  Ok - now on to my review of the actual recipe!!

I made this recipe pretty much as is - with a few exceptions.  I did not have the cereal so I made it without the cereal.  I increased the breadcrumbs to make up for the missing cereal (I just did this by site - not measurements).  I used italian seasoned breadcrumbs - rather than plain.  I forgot to cut the chicken breasts in half - darn it!  So, it took about 45-50 minutes to cook and that was my daughter's 1 complaint - that her chicken was too thick.  I did not pound them down at all because they were still a little frozen (next time I'll make sure I do this).

Overall - plates were clean and my daughter liked the taste of the chicken.  It turned out nice and juicy as most reviewers mentioned.  I will try this again.  However, next time I will try with the cereal (if I have it) and I will try baking it on a rack to alleviate the wet bottom (although it was very good that way too).

Thank you for the recipe - we enjoyed it!

text:
Meh. Allright, I guess.... My fiance thought this was "OK," but I can't say I agree. This was quite bland for my palate. I even added 1/4 c. grated Parmesan cheese to my cereal (I used Rice Krispies as directed) mixture and a t of onion powder to my flour mixture. Still blah. To cut some of the fat, I melted 2 T margarine instead of the 1/4 c. / 4 T butter called for. I did, however, still use the 2 T melted (butter) drizzle on top. Because my cheddar bay biscuits (Cookie) baked at 375 degrees, I ended up baking my chicken at this temperature also (I was concerned that adjusting the baking temp for the biscuits would yield poor results). I decreased the baking time to 25 minutes total and my chicken was SUPER moist! I found the coating to be oddly crisp. It reminded me of reheated breaded chicken. There was a slight crispness, but it wasnt good. On the flipside, clean-up was a breeze. I mixed my flour / seasonings in one large Zip-lock bag and my cereal mixture in another. As a result, I only had to dirty one bowl (for the eggwash)! Served with buttered corn, long grain & wild rice and Cookie's biscuits, this was a decent meal. I just don't think it will be a repeat in my house (sorry!). Maybe this will float your boat???? Thanks for sharing, Judy. :-)

text:
I wanted a quick and easy baked chicken recipe and this was good. The only things I changed was that I used 6 thighs, and panko instead of cereal because I didn't have any and I didn't use any butter because I figured I didn't need the extra calories. I also didn't have garlic powder so I substituted garlic salt but didn't use a whole tsp. I then sprayed my glass dish with Pam. The flour mixture made quite a bit and the leftovers seemed wasteful but oh well. The one egg+milk didn't seem like it'd be enough to coat all the chix but it was, just barely. I had to make a little more of the panko/cheddar cheese because I was running short. Not very difficult though. Overall it was definitely moist. It could've used a wee bit more flavor but the kids enjoyed it and I'll make it again. Thanks for sharing!

I've made many dishes from the recipes on this site but never felt compelled to leave a review until now. text:
This chicken is fantastic!!  My sister made me try it and I was skeptical at first - it was like nothing I'd ever made.  It turned out great the first time and every other time since.  A couple of things that I added to the recipe - when I mix up the flour mixture, I add more garlic, some cayenne pepper and some blackened seasoning.  It's not spicy, it just gives it more flavor.  Each time I've made it I try some new spices in it and it always turns out great.  I also use Italian bread crumbs.  I, too, spray the pan with cooking spray, but I like the butter on top, so I always do that.  This is a great simple, delicious recipe.  Thank you!

text:
We eat chicken several times a week, so I'm always on the lookout for something different. I didn't have any crispy rice cereal, so I used roughly crushed Ritz crackers and this still turned out nice and crispy. Because other reviewers thought the chicken lacked flavor, I floured the chicken and added the seasonings to each piece to ensure it had more spice than flour. I also added some cayenne pepper, and am happy I did, because it gave it that something extra. I also used nonstick spray on the bottom and drizzled butter on top, per other suggestions. My picky 4-year-old gobbled it up and my husband thought it was good too.  I will definitely try this again the next time I have rice cereal on hand and see how it turns out. Thanks for sharing!

text:
This was really a good recipe. A lot of times I try things and something goes wrong but tonight my chicken was really good! I did not have bread crumbs so based on other reviews, I tried goldfish crackers (I have them for my kids) crunched up w/the rice krispies. In addition to adding a tsp of onion powder, I also put a dash of paprika and parsley in the flour mixture, not sure if it was okay to do that but didn't make it taste bad. I was pretty liberal with the cheese too so I think that made it tastier. My chicken was very moist. Just used 3 boneless/skinless breasts. I used one egg (some said use 2, not needed for me) and everybody was right, the flour mixture is more than needed. I would probably have put half the flour in next time. I had lots of the cheese/cracker left over and just poured it over the chicken. I put Olive Oil in my pan to begin with, probably too much though (maybe about 2 tablespoons or so). The bottom was a tiny bit soggy. The butter had poured down there too and made it more soggy. But it was still okay, at least the top did not get too crispy/burned. Overall a great recipe for something (at least for us) a little different.

text:
I made this recipe with chicken breast tenderloins. I'm always nervous to use chicken breasts bc there is such a fine line between moist chicken and dried chicken bc I'm scared of undercooking it (thus always end up overcooking it).  So - tenderloins are the way to go for me. I took the suggestions of others and added the onion powder as well.  Chicken tastes great.  Easy meal to make.  I served it with my favorite side dish - HEB brand chicken rice! Also some green giant asparagus and I also baked some garlic cheddar biscuits.  It was a fantastic meal and since the ingredients are always readily available (except the cereal - I just omitted it) I was able to make dinner for three for under $10.  That's always a bonus!

What a delicious and juicy recipe!  A little fussy, but totally worth the effort.  The recipe tasted fine as is, but we learned you have to actually pat the chicken into balls with the 3rd mixture.  Otherwise, the cheese & toppings won't stick, and that's the best part!  You don't really need all that butter, either.  We used Pam to coat the baking dish.  I would probably bake at 400 for 30 minutes next time.  This seemed to take a little longer.  Served with rice & steamed broccoli, yum!
